                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anionic Redox in Rechargeable Batteries: Mechanism, Materials, and Characterization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Tianwei; Li, Xiang; Fu, Yongzhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2303191</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Compared with conventional pos. electrode materials in Li-ion batteries, Li-rich materials have a huge advantage of large specific capacities of &gt;300 mAh g-1.  Anionic redox mechanism is proposed to explain the over-capacity, which means anions can participate in the redox process for charge compensation.  The concept enriches the range and design considerations of high-energy-d. pos. electrode materials for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries, which therefore arouses extensive attention.  This review summarizes the progress of anionic redox in rechargeable batteries in recent years and discusses the fundamental mechanism that triggers anionic redox.  Moreover, the state-of-the-art materials involving anionic redox are illustrated, accompanied by the challenges for practical applications.  Furthermore, the common techniques for monitoring anionic redox are reviewed and compared for an advisable choice in future studies.  Finally, the consideration and discussion for designing stable pos. electrodes based on cationic and anionic redox are presented.  The perspective is highlighted and this review provides a basic understanding of anionic redox in rechargeable batteries and paves the way to develop high-capacity pos. electrodes for high-energy battery systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202301568"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>33</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">41</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2303812</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202303812</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D33%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D2303812%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D41%26author%3DM.%2BY.%2BShen%26author%3DJ.%2BS.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BRen%26author%3DT.%2BWu%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DW.%2BC.%2BLi%26author%3DA.%2BH.%2BLu%26title%3DQuasi-Zero%2BVolume%2BStrain%2BCathode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%2Bthrough%2BSynergetic%2BSubstitution%2BEffect%2Bof%2BLi%2Band%2BMg%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202303812&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c17755&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202303812&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quasi-Zero Volume Strain Cathode Materials for Sodium Ion Battery through Synergetic Substitution Effect of Li and Mg</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Ming-Yuan; Wang, Jing-Song; Ren, Zhouhong; Wu, Tao; Liu, Xi; Chen, Liwei; Li, Wen-Cui; Lu, An-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2303812</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type layered oxide material Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 is a competitive candidate for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Nevertheless, it suffers from the strong P2-O2 phase transition during charging to the high voltage regime, rendering drastic vol. variations and poor cycling performance.  Here, a Quasi-zero strain P2-Na0.75Li0.15Mg0.05Ni0.1Mn0.7O2 cathode is synthesized, which reflects the vanishing P2-O2 transition with a vol. change as low as 0.49%, thus resulting in the material an excellent cycling performance (83.9% capacity retention after 500 cycles at 5 C).  The low-vol. strain can be attributed to two aspects: (1) the Mg2+ riveted in the Na layer can act as a "pillar" to stabilize the crystal structure under the condition of sodium removal, thus restricting the structural changes under high voltage. (2) The entry of Li+ into the transition metal (TM) layer can mitigate the electron localization in the highly desodiation state and can effectively immobilize the coordination oxygen atoms, thus suppressing the slip of P2-O2 transition.  This study not only provides a new insight of Li and Mg synergetic substitution effect on the structural stability of P2-type cathode, but also an efficient avenue for developing cathode materials of SIBs with ultralow bulk strain.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202414627"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Che, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">21</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2203802</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">W-Doping Induced Efficient Tunnel-to-Layered Structure Transformation of Na0.44Mn1-xWxO2: Phase Evolution, Sodium-Storage Properties, and Moisture Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Qin; Zheng, Wanhao; Zhao, Along; Zhao, Yanan; Chen, Kean; Zhou, Xi; Zhang, Haiyan; Li, Qingyu; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Fang, Yongjin; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2203802</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na0.44MnO2 is a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries owing to its excellent cycling stability and low cost.  However, insufficient sodium storage sites still hinder its practical applications.  Herein, a facile strategy to induce the efficient structural transformation from the tunnel to the layered type of Na0.44MnO2 by trace W-doping for the first time is reported.  The W-doping not only enriches the sodium storage sites but also improves the cycling performance.  As a result, the phase-pure P2-Na0.44Mn0.99W0.01O2 demonstrates an enhanced reversible specific capacity of 195.5 mAh g-1 and energy d. of 517 Wh kg-1 at 0.1 C, accompanying superior cycling stability with capacity retention of 80% over 200 cycles.  Moreover, the W-doped samples show high structure stability in a moist atm. and can still maintain the original electrochem. performance after water treatment.  In situ and ex situ characterizations reveal the enhanced structural stability of the P2-Na0.44Mn0.99W0.01O2 electrodes.  This work provides a facile strategy on the structural engineering of transition metal oxides to induce the tunnel-to-layered structure transformation and could shed light on the design and construction of stable and high-capacity cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.3c02290"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Entropy Na-Deficient Layered Oxides for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS. Nano.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">13</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">12530</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">12543</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.3c02290</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D17%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D12530-12543%26journal%3DACS.%2BNano.%26issue%3D13%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BGao%26author%3DS.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BMei%26author%3DL.%2BNi%26author%3DJ.%2BGao%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DN.%2BHong%26author%3DB.%2BZhang%26author%3DF.%2BZhu%26author%3DW.%2BDeng%26author%3DG.%2BZou%26author%3DH.%2BHou%26author%3DX.-Y.%2BCao%26author%3DH.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26title%3DHigh-Entropy%2BNa-Deficient%2BLayered%2BOxides%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.3c02290&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c17755&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.3c02290&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Entropy Na-Deficient Layered Oxides for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Haoji; Gao, Xu; Zhang, Shu; Mei, Yu; Ni, Lianshan; Gao, Jinqiang; Liu, Huanqing; Hong, Ningyun; Zhang, Baichao; Zhu, Fangjun; Deng, Wentao; Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Cao, Xiao-Yu; Chen, Hongyi; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12530-12543</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium layered oxides always suffer from sluggish kinetics and deleterious phase transformations at deep-desodiation state (i.e., &gt;4.0 V) in O3 structure, incurring inferior rate capability and grievous capacity degrdn.  To tackle these handicaps, here, a configurational entropy tuning protocol through manipulating the stoichiometric ratios of inactive cations is proposed to elaborately design Na-deficient, O3-type NaxTmO2 cathodes.  It is found that the electrons surrounding the oxygen of the TmO6 octahedron are rearranged by the introduction of MnO6 and TiO6 octahedra in Na-deficient O3-type Na0.83Li0.1Ni0.25Co0.2Mn0.15Ti0.15Sn0.15O2-δ (MTS15) with expanded O-Na-O slab spacing, giving enhanced Na+ diffusion kinetics and structural stability, as disclosed by theor. calcns. and electrochem. measurements.  Concomitantly, the entropy effect contributes to the improved reversibility of Co redox and phase-transition behaviors between O3 and P3, as clearly revealed by ex situ synchrotron X-ray absorption spectra and in situ X-ray diffraction.  Notably, the prepd. entropy-tuned MTS15 cathode exhibits impressive rate capability (76.7% capacity retention at 10 C), cycling stability (87.2% capacity retention after 200 cycles) with a reversible capacity of 109.4 mAh g-1, good full-cell performance (84.3% capacity retention after 100 cycles), and exceptional air stability.  This work provides an idea for how to design high-entropy sodium layered oxides for high-power d. storage systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.2c00690"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Innocenti, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zarrabeitia, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bresser, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered Oxide Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Storage Mechanism, Electrochemistry, and Technoeconomics</span>. <i>Acc. Chem. Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>56</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">284</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">296</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Modulating Crystal and Interfacial Properties by W-Gradient Doping for Highly Stable and Long Life Li-Rich Layered Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Meng, Junxia; Xu, Lishuang; Ma, Quanxin; Yang, Mengqian; Fang, Yuzhong; Wan, Guangying; Li, Ruhong; Yuan, Jujun; Zhang, Xianke; Yu, Huajun; Liu, Lingli; Liu, Tiefeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2113013</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Stabilizing Li-rich layered oxides without capacity/voltage fade upon cycling is a prerequisite for a successful commercialization.  Although the inhibition of structural and interfacial changes is identified as an effective strategy, the battery community always seeks for a technol. flexible method to make it really competitive among the cathode.  Herein, the gradient W-doping within Li1.2Mn0.56Ni0.16Co0.08O2 (LLMO) is proposed to relieve crystal disintegration and simultaneously enhance interfacial stability because of the formation of Li2WO4 coating layer on the material surface.  This is mainly attributed to the scenario that partial Mn replacement by W can stabilize the LLMO structure and regulate the electrochem. activity of Mn element.  The W-doped LLMO (W@LLMO) possesses improved specific capacity and voltage stability (83.2% capacity retention and voltage retention of 94.9% after 200 cycles at 0.5 C).  Besides, a practical pouch cell based on the W@LLMO cathode presents sufficient gravimetric energy d. (318 Wh kg-1) and cycling stability (capacity retention of 87.7% after 500 cycles at 1.0 C).  This study presents an effective method to design robust Li-rich layered cathodes for next-generation Li-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202203216"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unexpectedly High Cycling Stability Induced by a High Charge Cut-Off Voltage of Layered Sodium Oxide Cathodes</span>. <i>Adv. Energy. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2203216</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202203216</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D2203216%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy.%2BMater.%26issue%3D6%26author%3DQ.%2BShen%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BJin%26author%3DX.%2BSong%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BQu%26author%3DL.%2BJiao%26title%3DUnexpectedly%2BHigh%2BCycling%2BStability%2BInduced%2Bby%2Ba%2BHigh%2BCharge%2BCut-Off%2BVoltage%2Bof%2BLayered%2BSodium%2BOxide%2BCathodes%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202203216&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c17755&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202203216&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unexpectedly High Cycling Stability Induced by a High Charge Cut-Off Voltage of Layered Sodium Oxide Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Qiuyu; Liu, Yongchang; Zhao, Xudong; Jin, Junteng; Song, Xiaobai; Wang, Yao; Qu, Xuanhui; Jiao, Lifang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2203216</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Initiating anionic redox chem. in layered sodium oxide cathodes is a prevalent method to break the capacity limit set by traditional transition metal redox.  However, realizing the "win-win" scenario of high capacity and high cycling stability is still challenging due to the high-voltage structural distortion and irreversible oxygen loss.  Herein, a Mn activation mechanism is unveiled in a novel P2-Na0.80Li0.08Ni0.22Mn0.67O2 cathode.  By elevating the charge cut-off voltage to 4.3 V, anionic redox is successfully triggered and partial oxygen loss enables the redn. of Mn upon discharge, thus activating more Mn3+/Mn4+ redox reactions in the following cycles and maintaining the total capacity almost unchanged.  In situ X-ray diffraction reveals a complete solid-soln. reaction with an ultralow vol. change of 1.04% upon cycling.  Consequently, the P2-Na0.80Li0.08Ni0.22Mn0.67O2 cathode simultaneously accomplishes a high discharge capacity (134.8 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C) and an unexpectedly long cycling life (capacity retention of 91.5% and 85.2% after 500 and 1000 cycles at 10 C, resp.).  Via systematic ex situ characterizations and theor. computations, the charge compensation mechanism upon Na+ insertion/extn. is elucidated.  This work broadens the horizons of current oxygen redox chem. and provides a new path to design high-performance layered oxide cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1039/D2TA08315A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Zn/Ti/F Synergetic-Doped Na<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> for Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Energy Density</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-step electrochemical in-situ Li doping and LiF coating enable ultra-stable cathode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Jiameng; Zheng, Chaoliang; Fang, De; Li, Jianling</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">82</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">228-238</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECOFG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-4956</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite of the higher energy d. and inexpensive characteristics, commercialization of layered oxide cathodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) is limited due to the lack of structural stability at the high voltage.  Herein, the one-step electrochem. in-situ Li doping and LiF coating are successfully achieved to obtain an advanced Na0.79Lix[Li0.13Ni0.20Mn0.67]O2@LiF (NaLi-LNM@LiF) cathode with superlattice structure.  The results demonstrate that the Li+ doped into the alkali metal layer by electrochem. cycling act as "pillars" in the form of Li-Li dimers to stabilize the layered structure.  The supplementation of Li to the superlattice structure inhibits the dissoln. of transition metal ions and lattice mismatch.  Furthermore, the in-situ LiF coating restrains side reactions, reduces surface cracks, and greatly improves the cycling stability.  The electrochem. in-situ modification strategy significantly enhances the electrochem. performance of the half-cell.  The NaLi-LNM@LiF exhibits high reversible specific capacity (170.6 mA h g-1 at 0.05 C), outstanding capacity retention (92.65% after 200 cycles at 0.5 C) and excellent rate performance (80 mA h g-1 at 7 C) in a wide voltage range of 1.5-4.5 V.  This novel method of in-situ modification by electrochem. process will provide a guidance for the rational design of cathode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2020.08.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vanaphuti, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ehrlich, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kisslinger, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unraveling Na and F Coupling Effects in Stabilizing Li, Mn-Rich Layered Oxide Cathodes via Local Ordering Modification</span>. <i>Energy.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have garnered unprecedented attention as an electrochem. energy storage technol., but it remains challenging to design high-energy-d. cathode materials with low structural strain during the dynamic (de)sodiation processes.  Herein, we report a P2-layered lithium dual-site-substituted Na0.7Li0.03[Mg0.15Li0.07Mn0.75]O2 (NMLMO) cathode material, in which Li ions occupy both transition-metal (TM) and alkali-metal (AM) sites.  The combination of theor. calcns. and exptl. characterizations reveals that LiTM creates Na-O-Li electronic configurations to boost the capacity derived from the oxygen anionic redox, while LiAM serves as LiO6 prismatic pillars to stabilize the layered structure through suppressing the detrimental phase transitions.  As a result, NMLMO delivers a high specific capacity of 266 mAh g-1 and simultaneously exhibits the nearly zero-strain characteristic within a wide voltage range of 1.5-4.6 V.  Our findings highlight the effective way of dual-site substitution to break the capacity-stability trade-off in cathode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202304067"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co-Substitution Enhances the Rate Capability and Stabilizes the Cyclic Performance of O3-Type Cathode NaNi0.45-xMn0.25Ti0.3CoxO2 for Sodium-Ion Storage at High Voltage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Chaojin; Yang, Lichun; Zhou, Chaogang; Lu, Bin; Liu, Jiangwen; Ouyang, Liuzhang; Hu, Renzong; Liu, Jun; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">O3-type NaNiO2-based cathode materials suffer irreversible phase transition when they are charged to above 4.0 V in sodium-ion batteries.  To solve this problem, we partially substitute Ni2+ in O3-type NaNi0.45Mn0.25Ti0.3O2 by Co3+.  NaNi0.45Mn0.25Ti0.3O2 with co-substitution possesses an expanded interlayer and exhibits higher rate capability, as well as cyclic stability, compared with the pristine cathode in 2.0-4.4 V.  The optimal NaNi0.4Mn0.25Ti0.3Co0.05O2 delivers discharge capacities of 180 and 80 mA h g-1 at 10 and 1000 mA g-1.  At 100 mA g-1, NaNi0.4Mn0.25Ti0.3Co0.05O2 exhibits 152 mA h g-1 in the initial cycle and maintains 91.4 mA h g-1 after 180 cycles.  Through ex situ X-ray diffraction, co-substitution is demonstrated to be effective in enhancing the reversibility of P3-P3'' phase transition from 4.0 to 4.4 V.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy indicates that higher electronic cond. is achieved by co-substitution.  Moreover, cyclic voltammetry and the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique demonstrate faster kinetics for Na+ diffusion due to the co-substitution.  This study provides a ref. for further improvement of electrochem. performance of cathode materials for high-voltage sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202301360"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mitigating Jahn-Teller Effect in Layered Cathode Material via Interstitial Doping for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">35</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2301360</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Gradient Boracic Polyanion Doping-Derived Surface Lattice Modulation of High-Voltage Ni-Rich Layered Cathodes for High-Energy-Density Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Fangkun; Liu, Zhengbo; Liao, Caijian; Xu, Xijun; Zhu, Min; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4903-4914</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of high-voltage Ni-rich cathodes can cost-effectively push lithium-ion batteries toward higher energy d. but suffers from major challenges with severe structural and interfacial degrdn. and compromised thermal robustness.  Herein, a multifunctional modification strategy (i.e., gradient engineering and surface lattice modulation) is rationally devised to establish a chemomechanically reliable single-crystal boracic polyanion-doped LiNi0.6Co0.2Mn0.2O2 (B-NCM) cathode that operates stably under high voltage (≥4.5 V vs Li/Li+).  It is found that introduction of a boron-based polyanion into Ni-rich cathodes could form a boron-polyanion gradient-doped structure and disordered layer phase on the surface of NCM particles, further inhibiting parasitic reactions and irreversible phase transition.  As a result, the B-NCM cells demonstrate capacity retention of 88.5% after 200 cycles at 4.5 V and stable operation at 60°C.  The current strategy employing gradient engineering and a surface disorder phase affords an effective and facile approach to boost the development of high-voltage Ni-rich cathodes and beyond.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/jcc.21057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hafner, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ab-Initio Simulations of Materials Using VASP: Density-Functional Theory and Beyond</span>. <i>J. Comput. Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2008</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>29</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">13</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2044</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2078</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/jcc.21057</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D29%26publication_year%3D2008%26pages%3D2044-2078%26journal%3DJ.%2BComput.%2BChem.%26issue%3D13%26author%3DJ.%2BHafner%26title%3DAb-Initio%2BSimulations%2Bof%2BMaterials%2BUsing%2BVASP%253A%2BDensity-Functional%2BTheory%2Band%2BBeyond%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fjcc.21057&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c17755&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fjcc.21057&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ab-initio simulations of materials using VASP: density-functional theory and beyond</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hafner, Juergen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Computational Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2044-2078</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCCHDD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0192-8651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  During the past decade, computer simulations based on a quantum-mech. description of the interactions between electrons and between electrons and at. nuclei have developed an increasingly important impact on solid-state physics and chem. and on materials science-promoting not only a deeper understanding, but also the possibility to contribute significantly to materials design for future technologies.  This development is based on two important columns: (i) The improved description of electronic many-body effects within d.-functional theory (DFT) and the upcoming post-DFT methods.  (ii) The implementation of the new functionals and many-body techniques within highly efficient, stable, and versatile computer codes, which allow to exploit the potential of modern computer architectures.  In this review, I discuss the implementation of various DFT functionals [local-d. approxn. (LDA), generalized gradient approxn. (GGA), meta-GGA, hybrid functional mixing DFT, and exact (Hartree-Fock) exchange] and post-DFT approaches [DFT + U for strong electronic correlations in narrow bands, many-body perturbation theory (GW) for quasiparticle spectra, dynamical correlation effects via the adiabatic-connection fluctuation-dissipation theorem (AC-FDT)] in the Vienna ab initio simulation package VASP.  VASP is a plane-wave all-electron code using the projector-augmented wave method to describe the electron-core interaction.  The code uses fast iterative techniques for the diagonalization of the DFT Hamiltonian and allows to perform total-energy calcns. and structural optimizations for systems with thousands of atoms and ab initio mol. dynamics simulations for ensembles with a few hundred atoms extending over several tens of ps.  Applications in many different areas (structure and phase stability, mech. and dynamical properties, liqs., glasses and quasicrystals, magnetism and magnetic nanostructures, semiconductors and insulators, surfaces, interfaces and thin films, chem. reactions, and catalysis) are reviewed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.50.17953"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Blöchl, P.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Generalized gradient approximation made simple</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perdew, John P.; Burke, Kieron; Ernzerhof, Matthias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1996</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">77</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3865-3868</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Generalized gradient approxns. (GGA's) for the exchange-correlation energy improve upon the local spin d. (LSD) description of atoms, mols., and solids.  We present a simple derivation of a simple GGA, in which all parameters (other than those in LSD) are fundamental consts.  Only general features of the detailed construction underlying the Perdew-Wang 1991 (PW91) GGA are invoked.  Improvements over PW91 include an accurate description of the linear response of the uniform electron gas, correct behavior under uniform scaling, and a smoother potential.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.3c02514"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Si, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">O3-type Na<sub>0.95</sub>Ni<sub>0.40</sub>Fe<sub>0.15</sub>Mn<sub>0.3</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode Materials with Enhanced Storage Stability for High-Energy Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">O3-Type Na0.95Ni0.40Fe0.15Mn0.3Ti0.15O2 Cathode Materials with Enhanced Storage Stability for High-Energy Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Lianzheng; Chang, Yu-Xin; Liu, Mengting; Feng, Yi-Hu; Si, Duo; Zhu, Xu; Wang, Xian-Zuo; Wang, Peng-Fei; Xu, Sailong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23236-23245</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">O3-type layered oxides with high initial sodium content are promising cathode candidates for sodium-ion batteries.  However, affected by the undesired transition metal slab sliding and reaction with H2O/CO2, their further application is typically hindered by unsatisfactory cycling stability upon charging to high voltage and poor storage stability under humid air.  Herein, we demonstrate a Fe/Ti cosubstitution strategy to simultaneously enhance the electrochem. performance and storage stability of pristine O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 cathode material, via employing high redox potential and inactive stabilized dopants.  The resultant Fe/Ti cosubstituted Na0.95Ni0.40Fe0.15Mn0.3Ti0.15O2 undergoes highly reversible O3-P3-OP2 phase transitions with a small cell vol. change of 2.8%, instead of complex O3-O'3-P3-P'3-P3'-O1 phase transitions in NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2.  Consequently, the cathode displays a high specific capacity of 161.6 mAh g-1 with an av. working voltage of 3.28 V and 81.8% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 5C.  Furthermore, the cathode material remains very stable after exposure to air for 7 days and even after soaking in water for 1 h, owing to the prohibition of sodium losing by elevating redox potential and contracting sodium layer spacing.  This work proposes an effective method to enhance the electrochem. performance and storage stability of O3-type layered oxide cathodes and promises advancing sodium-ion batteries toward large-scale industrialization.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref39" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2023.04.029"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unlocking High-Rate O3 Layered Oxide Cathode for Na-Ion Batteries via Ion Migration Path Modulation</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NaTi2(PO4)3 modified O3-type NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 as high rate and air stable cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Shengyu; Shi, Qinhao; Qi, Ruijuan; Zou, Xingli; Wang, Jing; Feng, Wuliang; Liu, Yang; Lu, Xionggang; Zhang, Jiujun; Yang, Xinxin; Zhao, Yufeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">441</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">141859</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2(NFM) were extensively studied due to their low cost and high reversible specific capacity.  However, the inferior rate and cycle performance, as well as the poor air stability severely limit its practical applications.  O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 is successfully modified with an unintermittent and thin NaTi2(PO4)3 (NTP) coating layer, which plays a crit. role in preventing the highly corrosive HF attacks from decompn. of electrolyte and subsequent dissoln. of the redox-active metal from the cathode particles.  Meanwhile, partial Ti4+ ions were doped in the bulk NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2, which can enlarge the interslab spacing.  DFT calcns. confirm the reduced Na+ migration energy barrier for the as produced sample.  As a consequence, the NTP coated NFM sample presents a superior rate capacity (103.1 mAh g-1 at 5 C), significantly enhanced capacity retention (77.5% at 1 C after 100 cycles), outperforming the state of the art literatures.  Besides, the air stability of the sample is well improved and the full cells deliver good cyclic performance when coupled with hard C, which will promote the large-scale application of O3-type cathode                 10.1021/acsnano.2c04702</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High-Rate, Durable Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Sb-Doped O3-Type Ni/Mn-Based Layered Oxides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Tao; Li, Siqing; Sun, Yuanyuan; Wang, Jeng-Han; Chen, An-Jie; Zheng, Qinfeng; Zhang, Yixiao; Chen, Liwei; Nam, Gyutae; Che, Haiying; Yang, Junhe; Zheng, Shiyou; Ma, Zi-Feng; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18058-18070</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">O3-Type layered oxides are widely studied as cathodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their high theor. capacities.  However, their rate capability and durability are limited by tortuous Na+ diffusion channels and complicated phase evolution during Na+ extn./insertion.  Here we report our findings in unravelling the mechanism for dramatically enhancing the stability and rate capability of O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5-xSbxO2 (NaNMS) by substitutional Sb doping, which can alter the coordination environment and chem. bonds of the transition metal (TM) ions in the structure, resulting in a more stable structure with wider Na+ transport channels.  Furthermore, NaNMS nanoparticles are obtained by surface energy regulation during grain growth.  The synergistic effect of Sb doping and nanostructuring greatly reduces the ionic migration energy barrier while increasing the reversibility of the structural evolution during repeated Na+ extn./insertion.  An optimized NaNMS-1 electrode delivers a reversible capacity of 212.3 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C and 74.5 mAh g-1 at 50 C with minimal capacity loss after 100 cycles at a low temp. of -20°C.  Such electrochem. performance is superior to most of the reported layered oxide cathodes used in rechargeable SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202303773"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Surface Engineering Through In Situ Construction of Co<sub>x</sub>B-Spinel Dual Coating Layers for High-Voltage Stable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>33</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">41</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2303191</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anionic Redox in Rechargeable Batteries: Mechanism, Materials, and Characterization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Tianwei; Li, Xiang; Fu, Yongzhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2303191</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Compared with conventional pos. electrode materials in Li-ion batteries, Li-rich materials have a huge advantage of large specific capacities of &gt;300 mAh g-1.  Anionic redox mechanism is proposed to explain the over-capacity, which means anions can participate in the redox process for charge compensation.  The concept enriches the range and design considerations of high-energy-d. pos. electrode materials for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries, which therefore arouses extensive attention.  This review summarizes the progress of anionic redox in rechargeable batteries in recent years and discusses the fundamental mechanism that triggers anionic redox.  Moreover, the state-of-the-art materials involving anionic redox are illustrated, accompanied by the challenges for practical applications.  Furthermore, the common techniques for monitoring anionic redox are reviewed and compared for an advisable choice in future studies.  Finally, the consideration and discussion for designing stable pos. electrodes based on cationic and anionic redox are presented.  The perspective is highlighted and this review provides a basic understanding of anionic redox in rechargeable batteries and paves the way to develop high-capacity pos. electrodes for high-energy battery systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202301568"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.                 10.1002/adfm.202303812</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quasi-Zero Volume Strain Cathode Materials for Sodium Ion Battery through Synergetic Substitution Effect of Li and Mg</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Ming-Yuan; Wang, Jing-Song; Ren, Zhouhong; Wu, Tao; Liu, Xi; Chen, Liwei; Li, Wen-Cui; Lu, An-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2303812</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type layered oxide material Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 is a competitive candidate for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Nevertheless, it suffers from the strong P2-O2 phase transition during charging to the high voltage regime, rendering drastic vol. variations and poor cycling performance.  Here, a Quasi-zero strain P2-Na0.75Li0.15Mg0.05Ni0.1Mn0.7O2 cathode is synthesized, which reflects the vanishing P2-O2 transition with a vol. change as low as 0.49%, thus resulting in the material an excellent cycling performance (83.9% capacity retention after 500 cycles at 5 C).  The low-vol. strain can be attributed to two aspects: (1) the Mg2+ riveted in the Na layer can act as a "pillar" to stabilize the crystal structure under the condition of sodium removal, thus restricting the structural changes under high voltage. (2) The entry of Li+ into the transition metal (TM) layer can mitigate the electron localization in the highly desodiation state and can effectively immobilize the coordination oxygen atoms, thus suppressing the slip of P2-O2 transition.  This study not only provides a new insight of Li and Mg synergetic substitution effect on the structural stability of P2-type cathode, but also an efficient avenue for developing cathode materials of SIBs with ultralow bulk strain.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202414627"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Che, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">21</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2203802</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202203802</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">W-Doping Induced Efficient Tunnel-to-Layered Structure Transformation of Na0.44Mn1-xWxO2: Phase Evolution, Sodium-Storage Properties, and Moisture Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Qin; Zheng, Wanhao; Zhao, Along; Zhao, Yanan; Chen, Kean; Zhou, Xi; Zhang, Haiyan; Li, Qingyu; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Fang, Yongjin; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2203802</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na0.44MnO2 is a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries owing to its excellent cycling stability and low cost.  However, insufficient sodium storage sites still hinder its practical applications.  Herein, a facile strategy to induce the efficient structural transformation from the tunnel to the layered type of Na0.44MnO2 by trace W-doping for the first time is reported.  The W-doping not only enriches the sodium storage sites but also improves the cycling performance.  As a result, the phase-pure P2-Na0.44Mn0.99W0.01O2 demonstrates an enhanced reversible specific capacity of 195.5 mAh g-1 and energy d. of 517 Wh kg-1 at 0.1 C, accompanying superior cycling stability with capacity retention of 80% over 200 cycles.  Moreover, the W-doped samples show high structure stability in a moist atm. and can still maintain the original electrochem. performance after water treatment.  In situ and ex situ characterizations reveal the enhanced structural stability of the P2-Na0.44Mn0.99W0.01O2 electrodes.  This work provides a facile strategy on the structural engineering of transition metal oxides to induce the tunnel-to-layered structure transformation and could shed light on the design and construction of stable and high-capacity cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.3c02290"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium layered oxides always suffer from sluggish kinetics and deleterious phase transformations at deep-desodiation state (i.e., &gt;4.0 V) in O3 structure, incurring inferior rate capability and grievous capacity degrdn. Herein, we report a P2-layered lithium dual-site-substituted Na0.7Li0.03[Mg0.15Li0.07Mn0.75]O2 (NMLMO) cathode material, in which Li ions occupy both transition-metal (TM) and alkali-metal (AM) sites.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  During the past decade, computer simulations based on a quantum-mech. description of the interactions between electrons and between electrons and at. nuclei have developed an increasingly important impact on solid-state physics and chem. and on materials science-promoting not only a deeper understanding, but also the possibility to contribute significantly to materials design for future technologies.  This development is based on two important columns: (i) The improved description of electronic many-body effects within d.-functional theory (DFT) and the upcoming post-DFT methods.  (ii) The implementation of the new functionals and many-body techniques within highly efficient, stable, and versatile computer codes, which allow to exploit the potential of modern computer architectures.  In this review, I discuss the implementation of various DFT functionals [local-d. approxn. (LDA), generalized gradient approxn. (GGA), meta-GGA, hybrid functional mixing DFT, and exact (Hartree-Fock) exchange] and post-DFT approaches [DFT + U for strong electronic correlations in narrow bands, many-body perturbation theory (GW) for quasiparticle spectra, dynamical correlation effects via the adiabatic-connection fluctuation-dissipation theorem (AC-FDT)] in the Vienna ab initio simulation package VASP.  VASP is a plane-wave all-electron code using the projector-augmented wave method to describe the electron-core interaction.  The code uses fast iterative techniques for the diagonalization of the DFT Hamiltonian and allows to perform total-energy calcns. and structural optimizations for systems with thousands of atoms and ab initio mol. dynamics simulations for ensembles with a few hundred atoms extending over several tens of ps.  Applications in many different areas (structure and phase stability, mech. and dynamical properties, liqs., glasses and quasicrystals, magnetism and magnetic nanostructures, semiconductors and insulators, surfaces, interfaces and thin films, chem. reactions, and catalysis) are reviewed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.50.17953"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Blöchl, P. However, affected by the undesired transition metal slab sliding and reaction with H2O/CO2, their further application is typically hindered by unsatisfactory cycling stability upon charging to high voltage and poor storage stability under humid air.  Herein, we demonstrate a Fe/Ti cosubstitution strategy to simultaneously enhance the electrochem. performance and storage stability of pristine O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 cathode material, via employing high redox potential and inactive stabilized dopants.  The resultant Fe/Ti cosubstituted Na0.95Ni0.40Fe0.15Mn0.3Ti0.15O2 undergoes highly reversible O3-P3-OP2 phase transitions with a small cell vol. change of 2.8%, instead of complex O3-O'3-P3-P'3-P3'-O1 phase transitions in NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2.  Consequently, the cathode displays a high specific capacity of 161.6 mAh g-1 with an av. working voltage of 3.28 V and 81.8% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 5C.  Furthermore, the cathode material remains very stable after exposure to air for 7 days and even after soaking in water for 1 h, owing to the prohibition of sodium losing by elevating redox potential and contracting sodium layer spacing.  This work proposes an effective method to enhance the electrochem. performance and storage stability of O3-type layered oxide cathodes and promises advancing sodium-ion batteries toward large-scale industrialization.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2023.04.029"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unlocking High-Rate O3 Layered Oxide Cathode for Na-Ion Batteries via Ion Migration Path Modulation</span>. <i>J. Energy. Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>83</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">53</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">61</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jechem.2023.04.029</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1039/D3TA03640E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hua, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bugday, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yasar, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Altin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Long, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An In Situ Dual-Modification Strategy for O3-NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> towards High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">35</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">18872</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">18880</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D3TA03640E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2023.141859"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Modified O3-type NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as High Rate and Air Stable Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>441</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">141859</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2023.141859</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NaTi2(PO4)3 modified O3-type NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 as high rate and air stable cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Shengyu; Shi, Qinhao; Qi, Ruijuan; Zou, Xingli; Wang, Jing; Feng, Wuliang; Liu, Yang; Lu, Xionggang; Zhang, Jiujun; Yang, Xinxin; Zhao, Yufeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">441</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">141859</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2(NFM) were extensively studied due to their low cost and high reversible specific capacity.  However, the inferior rate and cycle performance, as well as the poor air stability severely limit its practical applications.  O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 is successfully modified with an unintermittent and thin NaTi2(PO4)3 (NTP) coating layer, which plays a crit. role in preventing the highly corrosive HF attacks from decompn. of electrolyte and subsequent dissoln. of the redox-active metal from the cathode particles.  Meanwhile, partial Ti4+ ions were doped in the bulk NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2, which can enlarge the interslab spacing.  DFT calcns. confirm the reduced Na+ migration energy barrier for the as produced sample.  As a consequence, the NTP coated NFM sample presents a superior rate capacity (103.1 mAh g-1 at 5 C), significantly enhanced capacity retention (77.5% at 1 C after 100 cycles), outperforming the state of the art literatures.  Besides, the air stability of the sample is well improved and the full cells deliver good cyclic performance when coupled with hard C, which will promote the large-scale application of O3-type cathode material.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i10">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c17755?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c17755</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">XRD patterns, SEM images, XPS images, galvanostatic charge/discharge curves, CV curves, rate and cycling performance characteristics, single GITT titration curves, d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curves, average voltage and energy density evolution curves, Nyquist plots, in situ XRD patterns, lattice parameters of the <i>c</i>-axis evolution curves, ICP results, Rietveld refinement results, resistance values of Nyquist plots, and full-cell performance comparison data (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c17755/suppl_file/am4c17755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c17755/suppl_file/am4c17755_si_001.pdf">am4c17755_si_001.pdf (694.05 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div (function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();
